mw-body-content">\n</div>\n\t\t\t<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">List of wettest tropical cyclones by country</h1>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<div id="contentSub"></div>\n\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t<div id="jump-to-nav" class="mw-jump">\n\t\t\t\t\tJump to:\t\t\t\t\t<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, \t\t\t\t\t<a href="#p-search">search</a>\n\t\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><p>This is a <b>list of wettest tropical cyclones by country</b>, using all known available sources. Data is most complete for Australia, Cuba, Dominican Republic, Japan, Hong Kong, Mexico, Taiwan, Yap, Chuuk, and the United States, with fragmentary data available for other countries. The <a href="/wiki/Overseas_department" title="Overseas department">French region</a> of <a href="/wiki/R%C3%A9union" title="R\xc3\xa9union">R\xc3\xa9union</a> holds several world records for tropical cyclone and worldwide rainfall, due to the rough topography and its proximity to the Indian Ocean.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup></p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Global_tropical_cyclone_tracks-edit2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Global_tropical_cyclone_tracks-edit2.jpg/250px-Global_tropical_cyclone_tracks-edit2.jpg" width="250" height="125" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Global_tropical_cyclone_tracks-edit2.jpg/375px-Global_tropical_cyclone_tracks-edit2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Global_tropical_cyclone_tracks-edit2.jpg/500px-Global_tropical_cyclone_tracks-edit2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="8000" data-file-height="4000" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Global_tropical_cyclone_tracks-edit2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nA map of all tropical cyclone tracks, encompassing the period between the years 1985 and 2005.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Below are the records for each country above.</p>\n<p></p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc">\n<div href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Christmas_Island">Christmas Island</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Christmas Island">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gillian_Mar_22_2014_0310Z.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Gillian_Mar_22_2014_0310Z.jpg/220px-Gillian_Mar_22_2014_0310Z.jpg" width="220" height="245" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Gillian_Mar_22_2014_0310Z.jpg/330px-Gillian_Mar_22_2014_0310Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Gillian_Mar_22_2014_0310Z.jpg/440px-Gillian_Mar_22_2014_0310Z.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6200" data-file-height="6900" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gillian_Mar_22_2014_0310Z.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nCyclone Gillian</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Christmas_Island" title="Christmas Island">Christmas Island</a> is an Australian territory located in the Indian Ocean located at the summit of a submarine mountain, which rises steeply to a central plateau that is dominated by stands of rainforest.<sup id="cite_ref-C.26C_islands_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-C.26C_islands-14">[14]</a></sup> After rainfall and wind observations started on the island during 1972, only 13 tropical cyclones passed within 220&#160;km (135&#160;mi) of the territory between 1972 and 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-C.26C_islands_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-C.26C_islands-14">[14]</a></sup></p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<caption>Wettest tropical cyclones and their remnants on Christmas Island<br style="text-align:right;">0.67</td>\n<td>Denise 1975</td>\n<td></td>\n<td><sup id="cite_ref-Denise_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Denise-20">[20]</a></sup></td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cocos_Islands">Cocos Islands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Cocos Islands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:11U_Feb_25_2013_0350Z.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/11U_Feb_25_2013_0350Z.jpg/220px-11U_Feb_25_2013_0350Z.jpg" width="220" height="253" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/11U_Feb_25_2013_0350Z.jpg/330px-11U_Feb_25_2013_0350Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/11U_Feb_25_2013_0350Z.jpg/440px-11U_Feb_25_2013_0350Z.jpg 2x" data-file-width="8553" data-file-height="9825" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:11U_Feb_25_2013_0350Z.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nAlthough Tropical Low 11U in 2013 remained more than 120&#160;km (75&#160;mi) away from the Cocos Islands, wind shear displaced convection westward and over the islands for several days, resulting in record breaking rainfall.<sup id="cite_ref-11U_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11U-21">[21]</a></sup></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Cocos_(Keeling)_Islands" title="Cocos (Keeling) Islands">Cocos (Keeling) Islands</a> are an Australian territory of 27 coral islands that are formed into two large coral atolls and cover an area of around 36&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (14&#160;sq&#160;mi) of the Indian Ocean to the northwest of Perth, Australia.<sup id="cite_ref-C.26C_islands_14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-C.26C_islands-14">[14]</a></sup> Rainfall observations started on the islands during 1907, while temperature, wind and other records started in 1952.<sup id="cite_ref-C.26C_islands_14-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-C.26C_islands-14">[14]</a></sup> Between 1952 and 2005 27 tropical cyclones caused storm force wind gusts of over 90&#160;km/h (55&#160;mph) on the islands, while only four caused hurricane-force gusts of over 125&#160;km/h (80&#160;mph).<sup id="cite_ref-C.26C_islands_14-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-C.26C_islands-14">[14]</a></sup></p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<caption>Wettest tropical cyclones and their remnants in the Cocos Islands<br />\n<small>Highest-known totals</small></caption>\n<tr>\n<th scope="col" colspan="3">Precipitation</th>\n<th scope="col" rowspan="2">Storm</th>\n<th scope="col" rowspan="2">Location</th>\n<th scope="col" rowspan="2" class="unsortable"><abbr title="Reference">Ref.</abbr></th>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="col">Rank</th>\n<th scope="col"><abbr id="cite_ref-C.26C_islands_14-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-C.26C_islands-14">[14]</a></sup></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td>3</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">170.0</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">6.69</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Cyclone_Walter_(2001)" class="mw-redirect" title="Cyclone Walter (2001)">Walter 2001</a></td>\n<td></td>\n<td><sup id="cite_ref-22" id="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Bangladesh">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:02B_2015-07-29_0500Z.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/02B_2015-07-29_0500Z.jpg/220px-02B_2015-07-29_0500Z.jpg" width="220" height="286" class="thumbimage" has been the scene of the greatest tropical cyclone casualties in recent times. The country is quite flat and generally lies near sea level.</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="float:left; clear:left; margin:0.5em 1em 0.5em 0;">\n<caption>Wettest tropical cyclones and their remnants in Bangladesh<br />\n<small>Highest-known totals</small></caption>\n<tr>\n<th scope="col" colspan="3">Precipitation</th>\n<th scope="col" rowspan="2">Storm</th>\n<th scope="col" rowspan="2">Location</th>\n<th scope="col" rowspan="2" class="unsortable"><abbr title="Reference">Ref.</abbr></th>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="col">Rank</th>\n<th scope="col"><abbr title="millimetres">mm</abbr></th>\n<th scope="col"><abbr title="inches">in</abbr></th>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1</td>\n<td>1,051.2</td>\n<td>41.39</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Cyclonic_Storm_Komen_(2015)" class="mw-redirect" title="Cyclonic Storm Komen (2015)">Komen 2015</a></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Chittagong" title="Chittagong">Chittagong</a></td>\n<td><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td>2</td>\n<td>~300</td>\n<td>~12.00</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Cyclone_Rashmi" title="Cyclone Rashmi">Rashmi 2008</a></td>\n<td></td>\n<td><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td>3</td>\n<td>280</td>\n<td>11.02</td>\n<td>Monsoon Depression&#160;\xe2\x80\x94 Sep. 2004</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Barisal_District" title="Barisal District">Barisal</a></td>\n<td><sup id="cite_ref-PADGETTSEP2004_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PADGETTSEP2004-40">[40]</a></sup></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td>4</td>\n<td>253</td>\n<td>10.00</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Cyclone_Viyaru" title="Cyclone Viyaru">Viyaru 2013</a></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Patuakhali_District" title="Patuakhali District">Patuakhali</a></td>\n<td><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td>5</td>\n<td>227.2</td>\n<td>8.94</td>\n<td>Trop. class="mw-headline" id="Belize">Belize</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Belize">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>This country has terrain mainly across its southern sections, with elevations up to about 3,700 feet (1,100&#160;m).<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> The highest reported rainfall in what was formerly British Honduras occurred during <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Keith" title="Hurricane Keith">Hurricane Keith</a> in 2000 when 32.67 inches (830&#160;mm) of rain fell in a 24\xe2\x80\x91hour period at Phillip Goodson International Airport in <a href="/wiki/Belize_City" title="Belize City">Belize City</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Keith_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Keith-49">[49]</a></sup> It should be noted that equally heavy rains could have fallen during <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Hattie" title="Hurricane Hattie">Hurricane Hattie</a> of 1961 and <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Fifi" class="mw-redirect" title="Hurricane Fifi">Hurricane Fifi</a> of 1974.</p>\n<div style="text-align:right;">240.0</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">9.45</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/1964_Pacific_typhoon_season#Typhoon_Violet" title="1964 Pacific typhoon season">Violet 1964</a></td>\n<td>Paksa</td>\n<td><sup id="cite_ref-Mekong_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mekong-57">[57]</a></sup></td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td>3</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">30.5</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">1.20</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/1998_Pacific_typhoon_season#Typhoon_Faith_.28Norming.29" title="1998 Pacific typhoon season">Faith 1998</a></td>\n<td>Kompong Cham</td>\n<td><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Canada">Canada</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Canada">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:144px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Harvey1999092306GOES8IR.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/c/c1/Harvey1999092306GOES8IR.jpg" width="142" height="134" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="142" data-file-height="134" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Harvey1999092306GOES8IR.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nExtratropical cyclone Harvey near Nova Scotia</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Tropical cyclones are usually in transition to <a href="/wiki/Extratropical_cyclone" title="Extratropical cyclone">extratropical cyclones</a> by the time they reach <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Canada" title="Atlantic Canada">Atlantic Canada</a>, though occasionally they retain their tropical status. No tropical cyclone has ever hit Canada\'s Pacific coast.</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="float:left; clear:left; margin:0.5em 1em 0.5em 0;">\n<caption>Wettest tropical cyclones and their href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="China">China</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: China">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/China_tropical_cyclone_rainfall_climatology" title="China tropical cyclone rainfall climatology">China tropical cyclone rainfall climatology</a></div>\n<p>China is a mountainous country, which leads to rapid dissipation of cyclones that move inland as well as significant amounts of rain from those dissipating cyclones. <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Nina_(1975)" title="Typhoon Nina (1975)">Typhoon Nina (1975)</a> caused the collapse of two huge reservoirs and ten smaller dams when 1,062 millimetres (41.8&#160;in) fell in <a href="/wiki/Henan" title="Henan">Henan</a> during a 24\xe2\x80\x91hour period, which is the record for Mainland China. Typhoon Sam of the <a href="/wiki/1999_Pacific_typhoon_season" title="1999 Pacific typhoon season">1999 Pacific typhoon season</a> became the wettest known tropical cyclone to impact Hong Kong since records began in 1884, breaking a 73\xe2\x80\x91year\xe2\x80\x91old record.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> Precipitation associated with tropical cyclones and their remains can bring snow to <a href="/wiki/Tibet" title="Tibet">Tibet</a>. An early October 2004 tropical depression brought daily precipitation of 6 centimetres (2.4&#160;in) of liquid equivalent precipitation to Che-Ku county in the form of heavy snow, which was a new October daily precipitation record for both rain and snow. This led to a loss of 340,000&#160;kg of food, 230,000&#160;kg of forage grass, and 263 livestock in the snowstorm.<sup id="cite_ref-PADGETTOCT2004_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PADGETTOCT2004-42">[42]</a></sup></p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Soudelor_2015-08-08_0525Z.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Soudelor_2015-08-08_0525Z.jpg/220px-Soudelor_2015-08-08_0525Z.jpg" width="220" height="287" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Soudelor_2015-08-08_0525Z.jpg/330px-Soudelor_2015-08-08_0525Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Soudelor_2015-08-08_0525Z.jpg/440px-Soudelor_2015-08-08_0525Z.jpg 2x" data-file-width="7200" data-file-height="9400" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Soudelor_2015-08-08_0525Z.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nTyphoon Soudelor/Hanna</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<h3><span id="cite_ref-HK_79-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HK-79">[79]</a></sup></td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span id="Taiwan/Taipei"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Taiwan.2FTaipei">Taiwan/Taipei</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Taiwan/Taipei">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The mountainous island of <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a> province experiences an average of 1.8&#160;tropical cyclone landfalls each year.<sup id="cite_ref-BAMSapr2009_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BAMSapr2009-80">[80]</a></sup> Due to its rugged topography, Taiwan sees extreme rains from tropical cyclones, particularly in its central mountain range.</p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Typhoon_Morakot_Aug_7_2009.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Typhoon_Morakot_Aug_7_2009.jpg/220px-Typhoon_Morakot_Aug_7_2009.jpg" width="220" height="281" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Typhoon_Morakot_Aug_7_2009.jpg/330px-Typhoon_Morakot_Aug_7_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Typhoon_Morakot_Aug_7_2009.jpg/440px-Typhoon_Morakot_Aug_7_2009.jpg 2x" data-file-width="7200" data-file-height="9200" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Typhoon_Morakot_Aug_7_2009.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nTyphoon Morakot</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<table class="wikitable" style="float:left; clear:left; margin:0.5em 1em 0.5em 0;">\n<caption>Wettest tropical cyclones and their remnants in Taiwan<br />\n<small>Highest-known totals</small></caption>\n<tr>\n<th scope="col" colspan="3">Precipitation</th>\n<th scope="col" rowspan="2">Storm</th>\n<th scope="col" rowspan="2">Location</th>\n<th scope="col" rowspan="2" id="Cuba">Cuba</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Cuba">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Flora" title="Hurricane Flora">Hurricane Flora</a> of October 1963 drifted across Cuba for four days, leading to extreme rainfall across the mountainous island country. During the heaviest 24\xe2\x80\x91hour period of rainfall, 735 millimetres (28.9&#160;in) of rain fell at <a href="/wiki/Santiago_de_Cuba" title="Santiago de Cuba">Santiago de Cuba</a>. Total amounts of 2,033 millimetres (80.0&#160;in) over 4&#160;days and 2,550 millimetres (100&#160;in) over 5&#160;days produced staggering loss of life in Cuba, where over 2000 perished.<sup id="cite_ref-CUBARAIN_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CUBARAIN-95">[95]</a></sup></p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Hurricane_Dennis_on_July_7_2005_1550_UTC.jpg/330px-Hurricane_Dennis_on_July_7_2005_1550_UTC.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Hurricane_Dennis_on_July_7_2005_1550_UTC.jpg/440px-Hurricane_Dennis_on_July_7_2005_1550_UTC.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5600" data-file-height="7200" style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Dominica">Dominica</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Dominica">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Erika_2015-08-27_1725Z.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Erika_2015-08-27_1725Z.jpg/220px-Erika_2015-08-27_1725Z.jpg" width="220" height="286" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Erika_2015-08-27_1725Z.jpg/330px-Erika_2015-08-27_1725Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Erika_2015-08-27_1725Z.jpg/440px-Erika_2015-08-27_1725Z.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6000" data-file-height="7800" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Erika_2015-08-27_1725Z.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nErika near Dominica</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The islands of the eastern <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> are constantly threatened by <a href="/wiki/Tropical_storm" class="mw-redirect" title="Tropical storm">tropical storms</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hurricane" class="mw-redirect" title="Hurricane">hurricanes</a>, mainly between August and October. Dominica is a rugged island, with spots of elevation as high as nearly 4,750 feet (1,450&#160;m).<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> As <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Jeanne" title="Hurricane Jeanne">Hurricane Jeanne</a> moved through the region, 422.3 millimetres (16.63&#160;in) of rain fell during the 24\xe2\x80\x91hour period ending on the morning of September 15, 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-PADGETTSEP2004_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PADGETTSEP2004-40">[40]</a></sup></p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="float:left; href="#cite_note-WPCMAX-33">[33]</a></sup></td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Dominican_Republic">Dominican Republic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Dominican Republic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Noel_28_oct_2007_1530Z.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Noel_28_oct_2007_1530Z.jpg/220px-Noel_28_oct_2007_1530Z.jpg" width="220" height="286" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Noel_28_oct_2007_1530Z.jpg/330px-Noel_28_oct_2007_1530Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Noel_28_oct_2007_1530Z.jpg/440px-Noel_28_oct_2007_1530Z.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6000" data-file-height="7800" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Noel_28_oct_2007_1530Z.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nNoel near Dominican Republic</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The Dominican Republic, has some of the highest terrain surrounding the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a>, with Pico Duarte peaking at 10,700 feet (3,300&#160;m) above sea level.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> Most of the tropical cyclone rainfall totals on the list below are 24\xe2\x80\x91hour maxima, which likely underrepresent the storm total.</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="float:left; clear:left; margin:0.5em 1em 0.5em 0;">\n<caption>Wettest tropical cyclones and their remnants the Dominican class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Chuuk">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Elevations of the islands surrounding Chuuk lagoon reach a height of about 1,450 feet (440&#160;m).<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Chataan" title="Typhoon Chataan">Typhoon Chataan</a> led to excessive rainfall on this island from June 23&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 July 3, 2002, when a total of 939&#160;mm (37.0&#160;in) fell. During the time frame when Chataan was declared a tropical cyclone from July 1\xe2\x80\x933, 622&#160;mm (24.5&#160;in) fell, with 506&#160;mm (19.9&#160;in) falling on the 2nd alone at the international airport.<sup id="cite_ref-PADGETTJUL2002_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PADGETTJUL2002-112">[112]</a></sup></p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" id="R\xc3\xa9union_Island"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="R.C3.A9union_Island">R\xc3\xa9union Island</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: R\xc3\xa9union Island">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hyacinthe_25_jan_1980_0326Z_N6.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Hyacinthe_25_jan_1980_0326Z_N6.jpg/220px-Hyacinthe_25_jan_1980_0326Z_N6.jpg" width="220" height="213" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Hyacinthe_25_jan_1980_0326Z_N6.jpg/330px-Hyacinthe_25_jan_1980_0326Z_N6.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Hyacinthe_25_jan_1980_0326Z_N6.jpg/440px-Hyacinthe_25_jan_1980_0326Z_N6.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="580" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hyacinthe_25_jan_1980_0326Z_N6.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nCyclone Hyacinthe.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The mountainous island of R\xc3\xa9union has experienced several of the highest rainfall totals on record from tropical cyclones and holds the rainfall world records for 12, 24, 48, 72&#160;hours, four, five, six, seven, eight, nine and ten days as a result.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Gamede_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gamede-150">[150]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-E4_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-E4-151">[151]</a></sup> The 12 and 24 hourly rainfall records were set at Foc-Foc by Cyclone Denise in 1966, while an Unnamed Tropical Cyclone between April 8\xe2\x80\x9310, 1958 set the record for 48 hours at Aurere. <a href="/wiki/Cyclone_Gamede" title="Cyclone Gamede">Tropical Cyclone Gamede</a> between February 24\xe2\x80\x9328, 2007 came close to beating the records for 12, 24 and 48 hours before setting the records for three, four, five, six, seven, eight and nine&#160;days that were held by <a href="/wiki/Cyclone_Hyacinthe" title="Cyclone Hyacinthe">Tropical Cyclone Hyacinthe</a> 1980.<sup id="cite_ref-Gamede_150-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gamede-150">[150]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-E4_151-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-E4-151">[151]</a></sup> Hyacinthe 1980 currently holds the world records for ten and fifteen days with rainfall totals of 5,678 millimetres (223.5&#160;in) and 6,083 millimetres (239.5&#160;in) respectively recorded at Commerson Crater.<sup id="cite_ref-E4_151-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-E4-151">[151]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup></p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<caption>Wettest tropical cyclones and their remnants on Reunion island<br />\n<small>Highest-known totals</small></caption>\n<tr>\n<th scope="col" colspan="3">Precipitation</th>\n<th scope="col" rowspan="2">Storm</th>\n<th scope="col" href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Guatemala">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Agatha_(2010)" class="mw-redirect" title="Tropical Storm Agatha (2010)">Tropical Storm Agatha</a> in May 2010 became the second-wettest tropical cyclone in the nation\'s history when it slowly developed while remaining nearly stationary to the southwest of Guatemala, before turning northeast and dissipating across inland Central America.<sup id="cite_ref-Agatha2010_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Agatha2010-178">[178]</a></sup></p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<div class="thumb id="Haiti">Haiti</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Haiti">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Haiti that makes up three-eighths of Hispaniola,<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup> is a mountainous country that has experienced some of the most powerful hurricanes on record, including <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_David" title="Hurricane David">Hurricane David</a>. Its three mountain ranges have peaks as high as 8793&#160;feet/2680&#160;meters above sea level.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup></p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gordon1994111400GOE7IR.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/5d/Gordon1994111400GOE7IR.jpg" width="220" height="230" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="220" data-file-height="230" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gordon1994111400GOE7IR.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nGordon dropping heavy rainfall on Haiti along its frontal-like band</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<table class="wikitable" style="float:left; clear:left; margin:0.5em 1em 0.5em 0;">\n<caption>Wettest tropical cyclones and their remnants in Haiti<br id="cite_ref-ExtremeIndiaWeather_205-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ExtremeIndiaWeather-205">[205]</a></sup></td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Indonesia">Indonesia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Indonesia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:STC_Inigo_05_apr_2003_0625Z.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/STC_Inigo_05_apr_2003_0625Z.jpg/220px-STC_Inigo_05_apr_2003_0625Z.jpg" width="220" height="269" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/STC_Inigo_05_apr_2003_0625Z.jpg/330px-STC_Inigo_05_apr_2003_0625Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/STC_Inigo_05_apr_2003_0625Z.jpg/440px-STC_Inigo_05_apr_2003_0625Z.jpg 2x" data-file-width="7200" data-file-height="8800" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:STC_Inigo_05_apr_2003_0625Z.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nCyclone Inigo</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The precursor tropical disturbance of <a href="/wiki/Cyclone_Inigo" title="Cyclone Inigo">Tropical Cyclone Inigo</a> in April 2003 dropped heavy rainfall in eastern Indonesia. The rainfall caused <a href="/wiki/Flash_flood" title="Flash flood">flash flooding</a> and mudslides, primarily in Flores but also on <a href="/wiki/West_Timor" title="West Timor">West Timor</a><sup id="cite_ref-ocha1_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ocha1-206">[206]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Sumba" title="Sumba">Sumba</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bom_207-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bom-207">[207]</a></sup> In some locations, the depth of the floodwaters reached 5 metres (16&#160;ft). The Oessao River in <a href="/wiki/West_Timor" title="West Timor">West Timor</a> exceeded its banks, which flooded seven villages. In <a href="/wiki/Kupang" title="Kupang">Kupang</a> in West Timor, the system destroyed hundreds of homes and large fields of corn, bean, and rice crop. Heavy damage was reported near <a href="/wiki/Ende,_Indonesia" class="mw-redirect" title="Ende, Indonesia">Ende</a>, where flooding and mudslides destroyed 20&#160;houses and destroyed the roads connecting to East Flores. The city airport was flooded with one meter (3&#160;ft) of water, preventing aerial transportation and which left the city temporarily isolated. In <a href="/wiki/East_Flores_Regency" title="East Flores Regency">East Flores Regency</a> in eastern Flores Island, the system left 75&#160;destroyed houses, along with 77 severely damaged and a further 56 receiving light damage.<sup id="cite_ref-ocha1_206-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ocha1-206">[206]</a></sup></p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<caption>Wettest tropical cyclones and their remnants in Indonesia<br />\n<small>Highest-known totals</small></caption>\n<tr>\n<th scope="col" colspan="3">Precipitation</th>\n<th scope="col" rowspan="2">Storm</th>\n<th scope="col" rowspan="2">Location</th>\n<th scope="col" rowspan="2" class="unsortable"><abbr title="Reference">Ref.</abbr></th>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="col">Rank</th>\n<th scope="col"><abbr title="millimetres">mm</abbr></th>\n<th scope="col"><abbr title="inches">in</abbr></th>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1</td>\n<td>223</td>\n<td>8.78</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Cyclone_Inigo" title="Cyclone Inigo">Inigo 2003</a></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Larantuka" title="Larantuka">Larantuka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Flores" title="Flores">Flores</a></td>\n<td><sup id="cite_ref-gp_208-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gp-208">[208]</a></sup></td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Iran">Iran</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span island country of Jamaica can get lashed with rainfall by slow-moving tropical cyclones in the western Caribbean Sea. Its interior, the Blue Mountains, reach a height of 7,400 feet (2,300&#160;m) above sea level.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">[210]</a></sup></p>\n<table class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Japan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Talas_Terra_MODIS_picture_2011-09-02_(High_Definition).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Talas_Terra_MODIS_picture_2011-09-02_%28High_Definition%29.jpg/250px-Talas_Terra_MODIS_picture_2011-09-02_%28High_Definition%29.jpg" width="250" height="230" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Talas_Terra_MODIS_picture_2011-09-02_%28High_Definition%29.jpg/375px-Talas_Terra_MODIS_picture_2011-09-02_%28High_Definition%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Talas_Terra_MODIS_picture_2011-09-02_%28High_Definition%29.jpg/500px-Talas_Terra_MODIS_picture_2011-09-02_%28High_Definition%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="7432" data-file-height="6828" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Talas_Terra_MODIS_picture_2011-09-02_(High_Definition).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nSevere Tropical Storm Talas approaching Japan on September 2, 2011</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The mountainous island archipelago is constantly struck by typhoons recurving out of the tropics, which are normally in extratropical transition as they pass through Japan. Typhoon Namtheun of the <a href="/wiki/2004_Pacific_typhoon_season" title="2004 Pacific typhoon season">2004 Pacific typhoon season</a> holds the national 24-hour precipitation record with 1,317 millimetres (51.9&#160;in) observed in Kisawa village,<sup id="cite_ref-2004Japanrain_218-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2004Japanrain-218">[218]</a></sup> surpassing the previous record of 1,140&#160;mm (45&#160;in) set during <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Fran" title="Typhoon Fran">Typhoon Fran</a> in 1976.<sup id="cite_ref-1976fran_219-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1976fran-219">[219]</a></sup></p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="float:left; clear:left; margin:0.5em 1em 0.5em 0;">\n<caption>Wettest tropical cyclones and their remnants in href="#cite_note-PADAPR2003-233">[233]</a></sup></td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ryukyu_Islands">Ryukyu Islands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Ryukyu Islands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Rusa" title="Typhoon Rusa">Typhoon Rusa</a> caused 409 millimetres (16.1&#160;in) of rain to fall at Naze on August 29\xe2\x80\x9330, 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-PADGETTAUG2002_231-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PADGETTAUG2002-231">[231]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Aere_(2004)" title="Typhoon Aere (2004)">Typhoon Aere</a> dropped 314.5 millimetres (12.38&#160;in) of rain in the 65\xe2\x80\x91hour period ending at 1400 UTC on August 25, 2004 at Ishigakihima.<sup id="cite_ref-PADGETTAUG2004_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PADGETTAUG2004-74">[74]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/1957_Pacific_typhoon_season#Super_Typhoon_Agnes" title="1957 Pacific typhoon season">Typhoon Agnes</a> in August 1957 dropped 586.2 millimetres (23.08&#160;in) of rainfall on <a href="/wiki/Marcus_Island" class="mw-redirect" title="Marcus Island">Marcus Island</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-WPCMAX_33-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WPCMAX-33">[33]</a></sup> In 1972, <a href="/wiki/1972_Pacific_typhoon_season#Super_Typhoon_Rita_.28Gloring.29" title="1972 Pacific typhoon season">Typhoon Rita</a> dumped 31.87&#160;in (809&#160;mm) on <a href="/w/index.php?title=Okinoerabu_Shima&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Okinoerabu Shima (page does not exist)">Okinoerabu Shima</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-JTWC_Rita_1972_234-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JTWC_Rita_1972-234">[234]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Johnston_Atoll">Johnston Atoll</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Johnston Atoll">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Tropical cyclones occasionally threaten this central Pacific island. Hurricane Celeste of 1972 brought 6.21 inches (158&#160;mm) to the isle around August 19.<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">[235]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Korea">Korea</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Korea">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Korean_Peninsula" title="Korean Peninsula">Korean Peninsula</a> experiences typhoons regularly. Tropical cyclones which impact southern China also lead to, on average, five heavy rainfall events per year across the Korean peninsula.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">[236]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="North_Korea">North Korea</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: North Korea">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Very heavy rains fell across Tongchon and Kosong counties during <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Rusa" title="Typhoon Rusa">Typhoon Rusa</a> in 2002, where up to 510 millimetres (20&#160;in) of precipitation fell in a 5- to 10-hour period.<sup id="cite_ref-PADGETTAUG2002_231-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PADGETTAUG2002-231">[231]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="South_Korea">South Korea</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=56" title="Edit section: Mexico">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mexico_tropical_cyclone_rainfall_climatology" title="Mexico tropical cyclone rainfall climatology">Mexico tropical cyclone rainfall climatology</a></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Wilma" title="Hurricane Wilma">Hurricane Wilma</a> of 2005 drifted over the northeast portion of the Yucat\xc3\xa1n peninsula for a couple of days, dropping significant rains. A report of 1,576 millimetres (62.0&#160;in) was reported by the <a href="/wiki/Servicio_Meteorol%C3%B3gico_Nacional_(Mexico)" title="Servicio Meteorol\xc3\xb3gico Nacional (Mexico)">Servicio Meteorol\xc3\xb3gico Nacional</a> in Mexico,<sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261">[261]</a></sup> which is the wettest known 24-hour rainfall amount ever measured in Mexico. Second on the list is from <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Frances_(1998)" title="Tropical Storm Frances (1998)">Tropical Storm Frances</a> in 1998, which accumulated up to 1,019 millimetres (40.1&#160;in) of rain at Independencia in southern <a href="/wiki/Chiapas" title="Chiapas">Chiapas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">[262]</a></sup> Below is a list of the highest known storm total rainfall amounts from individual tropical cyclones across Mexico. Most of the rainfall information was provided by the Mexico\'s National Weather Service, Servicio Meteorol\xc3\xb3gico Nacional, which is a part of the National Water Commission, <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comisi%C3%B3n_Nacional_del_Agua&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Comisi\xc3\xb3n Nacional del Agua (page does not exist)">Comisi\xc3\xb3n Nacional del Agua</a></i>.</p>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Wilma_21_oct_2005_1625Z.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" Eight out of fourteen highest peaks in the world lie in the Nepalese Himalaya including the highest peak of the World, Mt. Everest (8848 m).<sup id="cite_ref-280" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-280">[280]</a></sup> During a tropical depression that affected the Indian Subcontinent in 2004, 51.3 millimetres (2.02&#160;in) of rain fell at Kathmandu airport in the 24\xe2\x80\x91hour period ending at 1200 UTC on October 7.<sup id="cite_ref-PADGETTOCT2004_42-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PADGETTOCT2004-42">[42]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Netherlands_Antilles">Netherlands Antilles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span id="Pakistan">Pakistan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=68" title="Edit section: Pakistan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Phet_jun_6_2010.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Phet_jun_6_2010.jpg/220px-Phet_jun_6_2010.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Phet_jun_6_2010.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a href="/wiki/Cyclone_Phet" title="Cyclone Phet">Cyclone Phet</a>, a cyclone making landfall in Pakistan in June 2010 as a deep depression</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Tropical cyclones for the <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Sea" title="Arabian Sea">Arabian Sea</a> usually affect Pakistan. Tropical cyclones from the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Bengal" title="Bay of Bengal">Bay of Bengal</a> can affect Pakistan, though they usually weaken by the time they reach the Pakistani coastline.<sup id="cite_ref-308" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-308">[308]</a></sup></p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<caption>Wettest tropical cyclones and their remnants in Pakistan<br class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=70" title="Edit section: Panama">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Inflow to the south of <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Mitch" title="Hurricane Mitch">Hurricane Mitch</a> brought impressive rainfalls to the Panama. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Veledero_de_Tole&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Veledero de Tole (page does not exist)">Veledero de Tole</a> recorded 695 millimetres (27.4&#160;in) of rainfall between October 22 and 31, 1998.</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Philippines">Philippines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a title="Cyclone Raquel">Raquel 2015</a></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Munda,_Solomon_Islands" title="Munda, Solomon Islands">Munda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Western_Province_(Solomon_Islands)" title="Western Province (Solomon Islands)">Western Province</a></td>\n<td><sup id="cite_ref-BoM_TCR_339-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BoM_TCR-339">[339]</a></sup></td>\n</tr>\n</table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="South_Africa">South Africa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=75" title="Edit section: South Africa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Cyclone_Leon%E2%80%93Eline" title="Cyclone Leon\xe2\x80\x93Eline">Tropical Cyclone Eline</a> in February 2000 dropped significant rains on portions of South Africa. The highest amount noted was 480&#160;mm (19&#160;in) at Thohoyandou.<sup id="cite_ref-340" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-340">[340]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Spain">Spain</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=76" title="Edit section: Spain">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The only tropical cyclone to reach mainland Europe was 2005\'s <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Vince_(2005)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hurricane Vince (2005)">Hurricane Vince</a>. It dropped 3.3 inches (84&#160;mm) of rain on the plain near Cordoba.<sup id="cite_ref-Vince_rainfall_341-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vince_rainfall-341">[341]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sri_Lanka">Sri Lanka</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=77" title="Edit section: Sri Lanka">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>A <a href="/wiki/2004_North_Indian_Ocean_cyclone_season#Depression_BOB_04" title="2004 North Indian Ocean cyclone season">tropical depression</a> in early October 2004 led to heavy rains across Sri Lanka. The maximum was measured at Galle where 117.2&#160;mm (4.61&#160;in) fell in the 24\xe2\x80\x91hour period ending at 0600 UTC on the 2nd.<sup id="cite_ref-PADGETTOCT2004_42-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PADGETTOCT2004-42">[42]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span id="St._Brandon,_South_Indian_Ocean"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="St._Brandon.2C_South_Indian_Ocean">St. Brandon, South Indian Ocean</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=78" title="Edit section: St. Brandon, South Indian Ocean">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p><a href="/wiki/2003%E2%80%9304_South-West_Indian_Ocean_cyclone_season#Severe_Tropical_Storm_Darius" title="2003\xe2\x80\x9304 South-West Indian Ocean cyclone season">Tropical Cyclone Darius</a> of New Year\'s Eve/Day of 2003/2004 passed about 45 miles (72&#160;km) west-northwest of the island. Rainfall over the 24\xe2\x80\x91hour period of closest approach was 135&#160;mm (5.3&#160;in).<sup id="cite_ref-PADGETTDEC2003_342-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PADGETTDEC2003-342">[342]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="St._Kitts_and_Nevis">St. Kitts and Nevis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-headline" id="Venezuela">Venezuela</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_wettest_tropical_cyclones_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=84" title="Edit section: Venezuela">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>A few tropical cyclones have skimmed the northern coast of South America over recent decades. <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Bret_(1993)" title="Tropical Storm Bret (1993)">Tropical Storm Bret (1993)</a> dropped 339 millimetres (13.3&#160;in) of rain in ten hours at <a href="/wiki/Guanare" title="Guanare">Guanare</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portuguesa_(state)" class="mw-redirect" title="Portuguesa (state)">Portuguesa</a>, Venezuela.<sup id="cite_ref-premlin1993_362-0" class="reference"><a
